~d:This year's TEDxGunnHighSchool theme is	"Be the Variable," the idea that individuals can work together to make an impact in the world by pursuing their passions. We will be hosting 10-12 Bay Area speakers from a diverse range of backgrounds like entrepreneurship, social media, engineering, technology, the arts, politics and education. Each talk will be 18 minutes long, and there will be breakout sessions during lunch where student can interact with speakers and participate in activities related to the talks. This experience will be a truly stimulating and inspirational for an audience of passionate learners. Anyone interesting in attending can register at www.tedxgunnhighschool.com or email tedx.gunnhs@gmail.com for more information.

!e:Gunn "Challenge Success" Event (Details Below): **07:00 PM** - **08:30 PM** (1 hour, 30 minutes)
~d:Join us for a panel discussion on how your student can use community college and/or taking a gap year towards a meaningful post-high school path. We will discuss the benefits and difficulties of these routes and engage in an interactive Q&A session. Our panel is comprised of recent university graduates and professors from local colleges. This event is a continuation of our last year's Challenge Success event, Diverse Paths to Success. This event reinforces that there are varied paths to success and every child needs to discover where his/her passion intersects with education and career.

!e:"Block Scheduling" Discussion: **07:00 PM** - **09:00 PM** (2 hours)
~d:Join us and learn more about the pros and cons of alternate or creative bell schedules at area schools!
~d:A panel of representatives from various local high schools and school districts, including Cupertino's Monta Vista, Palo Alto High, Piedmont, Woodside Priory, as well as our own Principal, Dr. Denise Herrmann, will share their experiences with and attitudes toward alternative scheduling. The panel will explain why their schools/districts opted to move away from a traditional high-school bell schedule, discuss both the benefits and challenges of different schedules, and address your questions.

!e:Community College (Why It Should Be On Your List): **07:30 PM** - **09:00 PM** (1 hour, 30 minutes)
~d:Have you underrated community college as a viable option? Honors College, challenging curricula, international diversity, and quality instruction are a few of the similarities that exist between Foothill College and 4-yr universities. Students need to understand the benefits a community college path offers, and we welcome you to this College & Career Center/Gunn PTSA sponsored event on why community college really should be on your list.
~d:
~d:As the cost of university degrees climb and admission competition escalates, attending college at one of our excellent local community colleges offers many benefits as you fulfill your general ed requirements or focus on a certificated program and employment. Join us for an overview of the resources, programs, education quality, and current transfer data.
~d:
~d:Our panel will include Foothill professors Simon Pennington (Art History), Brian Evans (Economics) and Lauren Velasco (Communications), and recent Gunn graduates whose academic paths have included Foothill or DeAnza Community colleges. This event is tailored to Gunn and Paly junior and senior students and their parents, but all are welcome.
~d:

!e:Yes! Stress Reduction Presentation (Registration Required): **07:00 PM** - **08:30 PM** (1 hour, 30 minutes)
~d:Freshmen and Sophomore parents:
~d:Feeling overwhelmed, busy, tense? Join us for a special interactive stress reduction and wellness presentation by the YES! (Youth Empowerment Seminar) organization on Thursday, October 15, 2015, from 7pm to 8:30pm in the Gunn Library. This is a special preview of the 4-week YES! program your Freshman and Sophomore students will be learning through their Gunn phys ed classes. Student stress is most effectively reduced when families encourage YES! principles at home.	San Francisco Bay Area YES! Director Priya Mayureshwar and Gunn parent/certified YES! instructor Anjali Vishwanath will be giving us an experience of the YES! program which has benefited more than 10,000 students in Bay Area schools. Over 7,000 students nationwide have reported an 87% "feel better rate" and an 83% improved academic focus after experiencing the YES! program. Now, it's your turn! Learn stress-busting, healthy lifestyle skills that work. Wear comfy clothes, bring a water bottle, and get ready to have fun and say YES! to stress busting.
~d:Please Note: There is no fee for this seminar, but spaces are limited and registration through Eventbrite is required. Register here: https://www.eventbrite.com/e/yes-stress-reduction-wellness-presentation-tickets-18700253963

~d:Adults 21 and over are invited to have a fun night out at the Inaugural Palo Alto Swing Dance, a fundraiser for the Gunn High School Music Department. ~d:

~d:
~d:- Tuesday: Movie!	Come watch Materials of the Future during flex! *Room TBA
~d:- Wednesday: Trash or Not Trash - Find out if you can sort more trash into the correct bins than your friend in 15 seconds at lunch on the quad! Winner gets a Cutie!
~d:

~d:
~d:- Friday: Make a Change - Sign petitions to help support students who want to make Gunn and the world more Green. Then, pledge to go green yourself at lunch on the quad!!!

!e:Challenge Success Talk By Julie Lythcott-Haims: **02:50 PM** - **03:35 PM** (45 minutes)
~d:TUDENT FORUM WITH JULIE LYTHCOTT-HAIMS	- Thursday during afternoon tutorial
~d:
~d:Julie Lythcott-Haims - Gunn parent, former Stanford dean, and author of the New York Times bestseller How to Raise an Adult - will be back on campus on April 28 to reprise her popular 2015 TEDxGunnHighSchool talk "Throw Out the Checklisted Childhood." Lythcott-Haims is a fierce critic of "helicopter parenting" and has spoken to parents nationwide about how overprotection, over-direction, or excessive hand-holding can achieve short term "wins" for kids but ultimately harms them. In her high school assemblies, she brings a compassionate approach to the stress and strain many kids experience today, and offers a different kind of checklist for achieving a meaningful and rewarding life.

!e:Bike Mobile @ Gunn - Free Bike Repair: **02:15 PM** - **05:15 PM** (3 hours)
~d:BikeMobile Comes to Gunn!
~d:
~d:FREE Bike Repairs for Gunn Students & Staff
~d:
~d:August 19, 2:15-5:15 near the Village
~d:
~d:BikeMobile will provide Free Bike Tune Ups for Gunn students and staff! They fix flat tires, adjust brakes and gears, and replace broken or worn out parts like chains, seats, and tires. They cannot replace missing wheels or gears. While BikeMobile mechanics work on your bike they'll explain how it works and how to keep your ride running smoothly. Space is limited, and bikes will be accepted on a first-come, first-served basis. Whether or not you have a bike that needs to be fixed, come learn about bicycle maintenance, bike safety, and more!

!e:Wind Ensemble & Symphonic Band Concert: **12:00 AM** - **12:00 AM** (1 day)
~d:The Gunn Symphonic Band and Wind Ensemble will present their first concert of the year in the new Palo Alto High School Performing Arts Center on Thursday, Oct. 6 at 7:30pm. (Spangenberg Theater is currently shut down).	The concert will feature an eclectic evening of music featuring several student soloists.
~d:Symphonic Band: The Lion of Lucerne by James Curnow, The Old Red Mill by Brant Karrick, Bosai Tree by Julie Giroux, and River of the Ancients by Michael Sweeney.
~d:Wind Ensemble: Fanfare for a New Era and Be Thou My Vision by Jack Stamp, First Suite in Eb by Gustav Holst, and La Oreja de Oro by San Miguel.
~d:Donations accepted at the door!

!D:02
!e:Sources Of Strength Discussion: **07:00 PM** - **08:30 PM** (1 hour, 30 minutes)
~d:Gunn and Paly families, students and community members are invited to learn about Sources of Strength, the wellness program based on building resilience at both high schools. Please join us, along with Lucille Packard Hospital's Dr. Shashank Joshi and Dr. Steve Adelsheim to participate in our spreading messages of hope, help and strength. All The Sources of Strength Teams (trusted adults) and Peer Leaders from Palo Alto High School and Gunn High School will be offering an experience for parents to take part in some of the routines of our Sources of Strength program as well as hear student testimonials about how they use the different parts of the Sources of Strength Wheel in their daily life. The Peer Leaders (students) are very excited to share with you all about what they have been doing this year and how this program continues to impacts their lives.
~d:Through Sources of Strength, our youth are identifying, discussing, and strengthening protective factors in their own lives, as well as working together to become agents of positive change and connectors to help those around them. As change agents, they will spread messages in person and via social media about the various sources of hope, help and strength available to the community. The Sources of Strength program actively creates a culture of increased awareness, compassion and support for all students facing the daily struggles of school and life and teaches strategies for building resilience and multiple sources of strength.

!e:Blood Donation Drive: **08:30 AM** - **03:30 PM** (7 hours)
~d:DO YOU WANT FREE ICE CREAM??? DO YOU WANT TO SAVE LIVES???
~d:The iMed Club and YCS Interact is working with Stanford Blood Center to bring back the blood drive!! You have to be at least 16 to donate, and need to turn in a consent form signed by your parents. Make sure you meet the height and weight requirements. After you donate, you will receive a certificate for FREE Baskin Robbins ice cream! Give blood for life!
~d:
